Needs deps.inline pinning or exact-link bisection. Quarantine count overall: **10 → 2**.
- Session 72 (2026-06-08): **Multi-stop navigation — stops visible on map (preview + nav), next-stop metrics, and confirm-gated skip-stop. Client-only.** Plan: `~/.claude/plans/greedy-skipping-wave.md`. **Problem:** the app already stored up to 3 `routeRequest.waypoints`, but once a multi-stop route was calculated the stops vanished from the map (only `route-planning` passed `waypoints` to `<RouteMap>`; preview + navigation didn't), all HUD metrics targeted the final destination, and there was no way to drop a stop mid-ride. **Approach:** derive leg boundaries client-side from route geometry + waypoints (no engine `legs` threaded through `RouteOption`/server/Fastify schema — dodges Gotcha #9; fully unit-testable). **Part 1 — stops on map:** wired `waypoints` into `<RouteMap>` in `route-preview.tsx` + `navigation.tsx`; upgraded the waypoint marker to a **numbered pin** (`constants.ts` `toMarkerFeature` stamps a 1-based `label`; `MarkerLayers.tsx` adds a SymbolLayer over a larger accent disc). **Part 2 — next-stop metrics:** new pure core helper `computeNextStopProgress` (+ `climbBetweenFractions`) in `packages/core/src/navigation.ts` — reuses `closestPointOnPolyline`/`findClosestPointIndex`/`polylineSegmentDistance`; "passed" semantics mirror `stripPassedWaypoints` so the shown next stop == the one a reroute keeps; distance = along-route to the next waypoint's snap, ETA = pace-scaled (`adjustedDuration/distance`), climb = positive deltas in the elevation window between rider & stop fractions. `FooterCard` now shows distance/ETA/climb **to the next stop** with a `STOP x of N` header + a subtle `to finish: <total> · <arrival>` line; no-stop routes render exactly as before (`hasNextStop:false` → fall back to totals). `navigation.tsx` computes `nextStopProgress` per GPS update. **Part 3 — skip stop:** "Skip stop" button on the stop header → `Alert.alert` confirm → `removeWaypoint(idx)` + reroute from current position to the following stop (or destination if last); disabled when offline. **Reroute stale-state fix (error-log #55):** `removeWaypoint` then `rerouteMutation.mutate` in the same tick used the stale `effectiveRouteRequest` memo (kept the skipped waypoint) — refactored the `mutationFn` to rebuild the request from `useAppStore.getState()` at execution time. **i18n:** 6 keys × en/ro/es (`nav.stopXofN`/`toFinish`/`skipStop`/`skipStopCancel`/`skipStopConfirmTitle`/`skipStopConfirmBody`). **Files:** `packages/core/src/navigation.ts` (+ `nextStopProgress.test.ts`, 10 tests), `apps/mobile/app/{navigation,route-preview}.tsx`, `apps/mobile/src/design-system/organisms/NavigationHUD.tsx`, `apps/mobile/src/components/map/{constants.ts,layers/MarkerLayers.tsx}`, i18n en/ro/es. **Verification:** `npm run typecheck` clean (3 workspaces); core suite **733 pass** (10 new + i18n parity); `check:bundle` HTTP 200; tester confirmed on the dev variant (numbered pins on preview + nav, next-stop metrics retarget after passing a stop, skip → reroute). **Minor deviation from plan:** skip button is **disabled (greyed) when offline** rather than hidden — clearer affordance. No server/DB/native changes; reaches installed apps on the next preview/production build.
- Session 71 (2026-06-08): **Post-ride impact card always showed "Kickstand / 0% tier progress" for every rider — fixed (server-only).** Diagnosed via `/review`. **Root cause:** the `award_xp` Postgres RPC returns snake_case JSONB (`total_xp`/`new_tier`/`xp_awarded`), but the `POST /v1/rides/:tripId/impact` handler cast the result straight to the camelCase `XpAwardResult` contract with `as` (a compile-time-only assertion, no runtime remap). Every camelCase read resolved to `undefined`, so `currentTotalXp` fell to `0`, `riderTier` to `'kickstand'`, and `totalXpEarned` to `NaN` — the `ImpactSummaryCard` then rendered tier 1 / 0% for everyone regardless of true tier. The single-word key `promoted` survived the mismatch, which is why genuine tier-up overlays still fired (the tell). Latent since the XP system shipped (migration `202604090002`, 2026-04-09); the route test never asserted on these fields, which is why it slipped through. **No data corruption** — `award_xp` updates `profiles.total_xp`/`rider_tier` server-side regardless of how the caller reads the return, so real XP/tier were always stored correctly; this was a pure display echo. **Fix:** new `normalizeXpAwardResult` in `services/mobile-api/src/lib/xp.ts` maps each snake_case key with safe numeric defaults, wired into the 3 read sites in `v1.ts` (ride/badge/streak XP). Audited every other `award_xp` caller (feed reactions/comments/shares, leaderboard, hazard reports) — all fire-and-forget, never read the result, unaffected. **Tests:** new `services/mobile-api/src/__tests__/xp.test.ts` (4 cases locking in the snake→camel mapping + null/partial-payload safety). `npm run typecheck` clean; the one pre-existing suite failure (`POST /v1/quiz/answer`, cross-test mock pollution) fails identically on baseline (verified via stash). **Deployed:** Cloud Build SUCCESS → Cloud Run revision **`defpedal-api-00089-9lc`** serving 100%, `GET /health` 200. Server-only — no app rebuild, no DB migration. See error-log #54. **Follow-up:** the `feedback.tsx` dashboard backfill should have masked this for advanced riders but didn't — suggests the live `get_impact_dashboard` RPC may have drifted from its migration (returns the XP fields per `202604090002`); worth a `pg_get_functiondef` check, though the deployed fix makes the card correct independently.
- Session 69 (2026-06-01): **Navigation fully localized (OSRM safe-mode turn-by-turn + nav HUD) + device-language auto-detection.** Driven by a tester report that Safe-route navigation instructions stayed English on a Romanian app. **Two-layer root cause:** (1) OSRM safe/flat routes ship no `maneuver.instruction` (no `osrm-text-instructions`), so `mapStep` hand-built an English fallback — fixed by new `apps/mobile/src/lib/maneuverInstructions.ts` (`buildManeuverInstruction(step, locale)` maps `maneuver.type`+`modifier` → localized `nav.maneuver.*` phrases with `{{direction}}`/`{{street}}` slots; U-turn dedicated phrase; unknown types degrade to a generic phrase; unnamed street → localized "the road"), threaded through `mapbox-routing.ts` `directPreviewRoute → mapRoute → mapStep` via the already-present `request.locale` (validated against `SUPPORTED_LOCALES`, defaults `en`). Mapbox fast routes keep their own `&language=`-localized instruction. (2) The **real** visible culprit: the nav HUD's `ManeuverCard`/`ThenStrip`/`FooterCard` render `getManeuverDescription()` — a *separate* hardcoded-English compact-label builder in `NavigationHUD.tsx`, NOT `step.instruction`. Localized it (now takes `t`), plus the "Then" prefix, metric labels (Speed/ETA/Dist/Climb), ETA "Now", the steep-grade pill, and all HUD a11y labels. **Font auto-shrink:** `ManeuverCard` description + both "Then" strips now use `adjustsFontSizeToFit` + `numberOfLines={1}` + `minimumFontScale` (0.55/0.6) so longer ro/es phrases stay fully visible on one line instead of truncating. **Device-locale auto-detection (`appStore.ts`):** `state.locale` + `DEFAULT_ROUTE_REQUEST.locale` now init from `getDeviceLocale()` (fresh installs follow the phone); new `localeExplicitlySet` flag set by `setLocale` so an explicit Profile pick is never overwritten by auto-detection on later boots; **persist migration v2→v3** — installs on the untouched `'en'` default adopt the device locale once, a non-English persisted locale is treated as an explicit pick and respected, and `routeRequest.locale` is reconciled with `locale` (heals the mirror-drift class that left turn-by-turn English even when the UI was Romanian). **Remaining EN in `navigation.tsx` localized:** guard-fallback screen, offline banner, hazard report banners (GPS-unavailable + recorded confirmations, with localized hazard-type label via `t('hazard.types.*')`), and all a11y labels (Free map/Recenter, Report hazard, elevation, menu, History/Community/Profile). Removed now-dead `hazardTypeLabels`/`HAZARD_TYPE_OPTIONS` usage. **i18n:** ~55 new keys per locale (en/ro/es) under `nav.*` (`maneuver`, `direction`, `maneuverShort`, then/eta/metrics, guard/offline/hazard banners, a11y, steep). **Safe-default routing reverified intact** — `partialize` still forces `mode:'safe'` every persist, migrate v<2 still resets, v<3 spreads `routeRequest` preserving mode; Safe pill active on cold start (`mode==='safe' && !avoidHills`, avoidHills default false); fast force-flip only in unsupported countries. **Tester confirmed on device:** instructions render Romanian, font shrinks to fit. **Verification:** `npm run typecheck` clean all 3 workspaces; bundle HTTP 200; targeted tests 124/124 (appStore 88 + mapbox-routing 25 + new maneuverInstructions 11). Pre-existing suite failures (weather.test, badge/share render crashes) are in untouched files. **Caveat:** ro/es maneuver strings are not yet native-reviewed — fold into the existing "Spanish/Romanian native review" watch-list item. Backend untouched (client-only). **Files:** new `maneuverInstructions.ts` + test; modified `mapbox-routing.ts`(+test), `NavigationHUD.tsx`, `navigation.tsx`, `appStore.ts`, i18n en/ro/es. **Release:** bumped to **v0.2.88 / versionCode 90** (commit `c7851b6`); built production AAB via `npm run bundle:production` (4m 2s, signed with the upload keystore — `keytool -printcert` confirmed owner `CN=Victor Rotariu`, SHA-256 `82:7C:FD:44:...:35:73`; dev-leak audit passed); archived `apkreleases/DefensivePedal-Production-v0.2.88.aab` (135.7 MB). **Uploaded and APPROVED by Google as the production release (2026-06-01)** — supersedes v0.2.85 (vc 87). Commits `7d0016d` + `c7851b6` pushed to `origin/main`.
- Session 68 (2026-05-26): **Spain routing support — RO + ES dispatch with country-aware OSRM endpoints, UI gating, cross-border notice, intra-region search, and effective-origin support resolution.** Shipped as 4 preview builds v0.2.79 → v0.2.82 to Firebase `early-access-preview`. **v0.2.79 (initial):** New Spain OSRM servers (`osrm-es.defensivepedal.com` for safety, `osrm-es-flat.defensivepedal.com` for climb-avoidance) provisioned upstream. **Core:** new `packages/core/src/countryCoverage.ts` — `SupportedCountry = 'RO' | 'ES'`, pure bounding-box `resolveCountryFromCoord` (RO `[20.26, 43.62, 29.74, 48.27]`, ES mainland + Balearics `[-9.40, 35.95, 4.33, 43.79]` — Canary Islands intentionally excluded for v1, no OSRM data shipped), and `isRouteSupported(origin, destination)` returning a discriminated union with `reason: 'origin_unsupported' | 'destination_unsupported' | 'cross_border'`. 16 unit tests covering Bucharest, Cluj, Constanța, Madrid, Barcelona, Palma de Mallorca, Las Palmas (null), Paris (null), null island, and cross-border. Both endpoints of a ride must resolve to the same country — OSRM data is partitioned per server. **Client dispatch (`apps/mobile/src/lib/mapbox-routing.ts`):** replaced the two top-level `OSRM_API_BASE` / `OSRM_FLAT_API_BASE` constants with `OSRM_BASES: Record<SupportedCountry, { safe; flat }>`. `fetchOsrmRoutes` now takes the resolved country; `directPreviewRoute` calls `isRouteSupported` up-front, and if safe is requested in an unsupported region it silently falls back to Mapbox Directions with `coverage.safeRouting=false` and `coverage.status='unsupported'` (defense-in-depth — UI should never let this happen, but a degraded route beats a thrown error). `showRouteComparison` forced to false for non-RO routes until Spain's `road_risk_data` is populated, otherwise "Similar safety to fast route" labels would surface against empty risk arrays. 6 new tests (ES safe → osrm-es, ES flat → osrm-es-flat, RO request still on `osrm.defensivepedal.com`, Paris fallback to Mapbox, RO→ES cross-border fallback, suppressed comparison for ES). 25/25 mapbox-routing tests pass. **Country resolution hook (`apps/mobile/src/hooks/useResolvedCountry.ts`):** reads `routeRequest.origin` + `destination` from Zustand, computes `{ originCountry, destinationCountry, routeSupported, unsupportedReason }`, side-effect mirrors the origin country to `routeRequest.countryHint` (so any downstream consumer reading the legacy hint sees the truth, not the persisted default `'RO'`). **UI gating (`apps/mobile/app/route-planning.tsx`):** when `!routeSupported`, the Safe/Fast/Flat 3-way pill row is hidden and replaced by a coverage-notice strip with one of three messages — `coverageCrossBorder`, `coverageDestinationUnsupported`, `coverageOriginUnsupported` — each i18n'd EN + RO (Spanish locale deferred to a follow-up). New effect force-flips mode to `'fast'` and clears `routePreview` when the rider drifts out of coverage so they can't accidentally request a Safe/Flat profile. **route-preview** mode-cycle pill (Safe→Fast→Flat) now disables on the unsupported branch via `modeCycleDisabled = isCyclingMode || !resolvedCountry.routeSupported`. **`SUPPORTED_COUNTRIES` in `mapbox-search.ts`** gains `'ES'` (was `['BR', 'RO']` → `['BR', 'RO', 'ES']`). **Server alignment (`services/mobile-api/src/config.ts`):** new `safeOsrmEsBaseUrl` + `safeOsrmEsFlatBaseUrl` env vars defaulting to the same `osrm-es*` URLs as the client; `SUPPORTED_SAFE_COUNTRIES` default `['RO', 'ES']`. `customOsrm.ts` calls `isRouteSupported` and dispatches by country (throws typed error on unsupported pairs); `loopRoute.ts` (onboarding habit-engine loop generation) routes by `resolveCountryFromCoord(origin)`. `.env.example` updated with all four OSRM URLs. Cloud Run env needs `SUPPORTED_SAFE_COUNTRIES=RO,ES` to be set on the next revision; the defaults already give the right behaviour without it. **TypeScript pitfall hit:** in `customOsrm.ts`, `if (!support.supported)` failed to narrow the discriminated union (TS reported "Property 'reason' does not exist on type `{ supported: true; country }`"), but `if (support.supported !== true)` narrowed correctly. Possibly an interaction with `readonly` discriminants in TS 5.8; non-blocking workaround. **Open question NOT addressed in code:** `road_risk_data` is empty for Spain — the comparison suppression handles this gracefully, but `RiskDistributionCard` on route-preview will simply render nothing for ES rides (existing `segments.length > 0` gate). When Spain risk data ships, the `support.country === 'RO'` check in `directPreviewRoute` should expand to `support.country in {'RO', 'ES'}`. **Verification:** `npm run typecheck` clean all three workspaces; `npm run check:bundle` HTTP 200; **151 tests in changed files pass** (16 countryCoverage + 25 mapbox-routing + 22 mapbox-search + 88 appStore); 504 server tests pass. **v0.2.80 (search default fix, tester reported "search still returns Romanian-only"):** root cause was `DEFAULT_ROUTE_REQUEST.countryHint = 'RO'` in `appStore.ts` — that value got persisted in Zustand and piped straight into Mapbox's `country=` filter on every autocomplete call. Two fixes: (a) changed default to `undefined` so a cold-start search isn't pre-restricted; (b) `useResolvedCountry` hook now actively CLEARS `countryHint` to undefined when origin resolves outside RO/ES (it was previously leaving the stale value), so a rider travelling to France no longer gets Romanian autocomplete forever. **v0.2.81 (search expansion fix, tester reported still no Spanish results when physically in Romania):** the v0.2.80 fix only helped during the GPS-pending window; once GPS landed in Romania, `countryHint='RO'` again locked Mapbox to Romania. Real fix in `mapbox-search.ts`: whenever `countryHint` resolves to ANY of the routing countries (RO or ES), expand the Mapbox `country` param to BOTH (`country=RO,ES`) for autocomplete AND reverse-geocode. New `ROUTING_COUNTRIES`/`ROUTING_COUNTRY_SET`/`expandSearchCountries` helper. Now a Romanian rider can autocomplete "Madrid" and a Spanish rider can autocomplete "Bucharest", proximity-bias keeps local results on top. Riders outside RO+ES still get unrestricted global search. **v0.2.82 (cross-border false-positive, tester reported "cross-border banner triggers on intra-Spain routes"):** root cause was `useResolvedCountry` reading `routeRequest.origin` (physical GPS) when the actual route uses `getPreviewOrigin(routeRequest) = startOverride ?? origin`. A Romanian tester using "Change start" to test intra-Spain routes (Change-Start=Madrid, Destination=Barcelona) saw origin=Bucharest + destination=Madrid → cross_border banner, even though the routed ride was Madrid → Barcelona. Fix: hook now resolves country support from the EFFECTIVE routing origin (matches what the OSRM dispatcher does). The `countryHint` side-effect for search biasing stays on the PHYSICAL origin — search should follow where you are, not where you're planning from. Tester confirmed working. **TypeScript pitfall hit:** in `customOsrm.ts`, `if (!support.supported)` failed to narrow the discriminated union (TS reported "Property 'reason' does not exist on type `{ supported: true; country }`"), but `if (support.supported !== true)` narrowed correctly. Possibly an interaction with `readonly` discriminants in TS 5.8; non-blocking workaround. **Build script gotcha caught + worth a memory entry:** `scripts/build-preview.sh` defaults `SRC=C:/dev/defpedal` (main repo). When running from a worktree the first build accidentally shipped the unrelated v0.2.78 main code; have to invoke as `SRC="$(pwd)" npm run build:preview` or the equivalent absolute path. **Open question NOT addressed in code:** `road_risk_data` is empty for Spain — the comparison suppression handles this gracefully, but `RiskDistributionCard` on route-preview will simply render nothing for ES rides (existing `segments.length > 0` gate). When Spain risk data ships, the `support.country === 'RO'` check in `directPreviewRoute` should expand to `support.country in {'RO', 'ES'}`. **Verification:** `npm run typecheck` clean all three workspaces (each iteration); `npm run check:bundle` HTTP 200 (each); **151 tests in changed files pass** (16 countryCoverage + 25 mapbox-routing + 22 mapbox-search + 88 appStore); 504 server tests pass. **Tester confirmed v0.2.82 works** — intra-Spain routing, cross-country search both functional. **Spanish (`es`) locale deferred** — banners ship EN + RO only this session. **Documentation updated this session:** progress.md (this entry); CLAUDE.md Tech Stack (OSRM rows) + Working Features. **Server NOT yet deployed** — `customOsrm.ts` + `loopRoute.ts` + `config.ts` updated; needs a new Cloud Run revision so server-side OSRM dispatch knows about Spain (mobile fetches routes client-side most of the time, but `/v1/routes/preview` + onboarding loop-route still call server-side OSRM).
- Session 59 (2026-05-23): **Play Store review prompt — two-stage sentiment funnel shipped end-to-end (plan → core → store → native wrapper → card → screen wire-up → opt-out + dev hook + cleanup).** Driven by user request "make a plan how to ask for play store review", iterated through one round of UX feedback (mascot too small, text cramped, perceived load delay). **Strategy:** Stage 1 = our own sentiment card with three answers (Loving it / Could be better / Later) → Stage 2 = native Play `ReviewManager` via `expo-store-review` only on positive sentiment, so unhappy users get routed to in-app feedback instead of burning the Play review quota on a 1-star public rating. **Core (`packages/core/src/reviewEligibility.ts` + 48 tests):** pure gating module owning all thresholds (7-day install age, 3-ride floor, 90/30/365-day cooldowns by sentiment, 3-prompt lifetime cap, 3-soft-dismiss escalation, 24h post-error window). `evaluateReviewEligibility(state, ctx)` returns the trigger label or `null`; `recordPromptShown/Sentiment/SoftDismiss/Rated/Error`, `ensureInstalledAt`, `setOptedOut` are pure reducers so the Zustand slice composes from them. **One test caught a real bug pre-merge:** `daysBetween(null, ...) → Infinity` is the right convention for cooldown timestamps but wrong for `installedAt` (means "we haven't seeded a first eligibility check yet, treat as too new") — added an explicit `state.installedAt === null` short-circuit in the helper. **Zustand slice (`apps/mobile/src/store/appStore.ts`):** `reviewPromptState: ReviewPromptState` + `completedRideCount: number` fields, 7 actions (`seedReviewInstallAtIfMissing`, `markReviewPromptShown`, `setReviewSentiment`, `markReviewSoftDismiss`, `markReviewRated`, `markReviewError`, `setReviewOptOut`). `completedRideCount` increments **only on the real `navigating → awaiting_feedback` transition** inside `finishNavigation` (not on the idempotent reconciliation branch — discarded rides don't count). Both fields persisted, intentionally **NOT** reset in `resetUserScopedState` — Play's review quota is per-Play-account on the device, not per-app-account, so user sign-out/sign-in on the same handset must not reopen the prompt window. Comment in-store documents this. **Native wrapper (`apps/mobile/src/lib/review-prompt.ts`):** installed `expo-store-review@~55.0.14` via `npx expo install`; `requestPlayStoreReview()` guards on `hasExpoNativeModule('ExpoStoreReview')` (the generic arch-independent primitive from session 56 — covers bridgeless preview/production builds where `NativeModules.ExpoStoreReview` would be undefined, error-log #21), lazy `require('expo-store-review')`, falls back to `Linking.openURL('https://play.google.com/store/apps/details?id=com.defensivepedal.mobile')` when the native sheet isn't available. Returns `'native' | 'fallback' | 'failed'` discriminator. **Important behavioural note baked into a comment:** Google's `ReviewManager` gives no signal about whether the sheet actually rendered (quota-throttled silently) — caller must treat any non-throw as "the user has been given the path" and respect the long cooldown, NOT re-prompt expecting "real" engagement. **`ReviewPromptCard` organism (`apps/mobile/src/design-system/organisms/ReviewPromptCard.tsx`):** 4-stage state machine (`sentiment → positive → negative → thanks`), dismissible (small ✕ → records `'later'` sentiment), records "prompt shown" once on mount + "soft dismiss" on unmount if no explicit answer, fires native call optimistically (sets `rated: true` before the awaitable resolves so even a silent quota-failure still respects the year-long mute). Uses new `<Mascot pose="high-five">` — added `'high-five'` to `MascotPose` union + `mascotPoses` token map (user-supplied `pedal-high-five.png` was already in `assets/mascot/`). **Layout iteration this session:** v1 was side-by-side (mascot left at `size="sm"`/80px, content right), tester reported "too small, text cramped, slow to appear" — v2 switched to **stacked column layout** (mascot centered at `size="md"`/120px above the title/body, text full-width and `textAlign: 'center'`, buttons stack vertically full-width), and added an off-screen `<Image>` preload mount in `feedback.tsx` (1×1, opacity 0) so the mascot bitmap decodes during the impact step well before the post-submit card mounts — kills the perceived load delay. **Wired into `feedback.tsx`:** seeds `installedAt` lazily on first AWAITING_FEEDBACK entry (so the 7-day install gate counts from "first completed ride", which is slightly more conservative than first app open — fine). On rating submit with `rating >= 4`, evaluates `evaluateReviewEligibility` with live suppressors (`isOffline` from `useConnectivity`, `hadRerouteOnLastRide` derived from `navigationSession.lastRerouteAt`) — if eligible, renders the card inline inside the existing "Thank you!" panel above the Done button (NOT as a blocking modal; the card is the natural pause point). **Profile opt-out:** "Play Store review prompts" `SettingRow` under Profile > Display, EN + RO copy, wired to `reviewPromptState.optedOut` via `setReviewOptOut(!enabled)`. **Dev hook:** added a "Review prompt (dev)" card to `apps/mobile/app/diagnostics.tsx` that pre-seeds `installedAt` to 8 days ago, resets sentiment state, and forces `completedRideCount = 3` so the trial path doesn't require a 7-day calendar wait. Gated on `mobileEnv.appEnv !== 'production'` so it's visible on dev + preview but hidden in production builds. Live state line shows `installedAt` and the bookkeeping fields so the tester can verify the seed actually wrote. **Three follow-ups landed in the same PR:** (1) `ErrorBoundary.componentDidCatch` now calls `useAppStore.getState().markReviewError()` inside a try/catch (so a Zustand failure can never break the error boundary itself) — closes the loop on the 24h post-error suppression window; (2) trigger label in `feedback.tsx` is now derived from a ladder (`tier_promotion > badge_unlocked > co2_milestone > positive_feedback`) so telemetry attributes the prompt to the strongest ride event without adding more card surfaces (one surface — feedback screen — keeps pestering risk bounded); (3) dev diagnostics card gated off in production. **i18n:** added 13 new keys in both EN + RO (`reviewPrompt.*` for the four card stages and the dismiss a11y label, `profile.reviewPrompts` + `On/Off` descriptions for the toggle). **Manual trial path executed on dev variant** (production-published Play listing means `'fallback'` path runs since `com.defensivepedal.mobile.dev` isn't published — expected, documented in the wrapper comment). Tester confirmed: card appears reliably after seed + 5-star rating, mascot loads without lag, layout breathes. **Pitfalls hit during the trial:** (a) USB `adb reverse` had silently dropped — `adb reverse --list` returned empty, restored with explicit re-apply; (b) v1 of the dev diagnostics card displayed only `promptCount`/`completedRideCount`/sentiment, but `Math.max(rides, 3)` clamp meant rides didn't change visibly when the tester already had ≥3 — added `installedAt` to the visible state line so the seed action produces an observable diff. **No new CLAUDE.md error-log entries** — the architecture is conventional and the only "gotchas" (silent ReviewManager quota, bridgeless native-module guard) are documented in existing CLAUDE.md sections and the file-level comments. **Verification:** `npm run typecheck` clean all three workspaces; `npm run check:bundle` HTTP 200; `npm run lint:check` 0 regressions; **core tests 48/48 + appStore tests 88/88 pass**. **Backend untouched** — entirely client-side feature; still on Cloud Run revision `defpedal-api-00081-69b` from session 58. **Documentation updated this session:** progress.md (this entry); CLAUDE.md Working Features section (new entry). **Commits:** TBD.
- Session 58 (2026-05-23): **City suggestions — shipped end-to-end (plan → DB → API → mobile → live).** Multi-agent team produced `docs/plans/city-suggestions.md` then I implemented it. **DB:** new `public.city_suggestions` table (PostGIS `geography(Point,4326)` + lat/lon mirrors, `body` CHECK 1–500, status enum, `client_submitted_at` for offline-queue latency, RLS = own-row insert by full users only + own-row select, no public read, no UPDATE/DELETE policies — admin uses service role) via migration `202605230002_create_city_suggestions.sql`. **API:** `POST /v1/city-suggestions` behind `requireFullUser` (anonymous rejected) with a dedicated `citySuggestion` rate-limit bucket (5/hour, env-overridable), full Fastify request + response JSON Schemas to dodge Gotcha #9, plus a stub `GET /v1/city-suggestions/nearby` returning `[]` so the future display-surface URL is already stable. Shipped on Cloud Run revision `defpedal-api-00081-69b`. **Mobile:** unified `RouteMap` crosshair into `crosshairMode: 'hazard' | 'suggestion' | null` (kept `hazardPlacementMode` as a deprecated one-release alias so route-planning's hazard flow didn't have to migrate in the same PR); new `CitySuggestionSheet` organism (multiline 500-char input with counter that turns warning-coloured at 450); new `useSubmitCitySuggestion` hook that always enqueues via the offline queue (offline-safe by design, mirrors the hazard-vote pattern); persisted `recentCitySuggestions` slice (cap 5, included in `resetUserScopedState` AND `partialize` in the same commit per error-log #30); EN + RO i18n keys for the whole surface. **FAB location: user revised scope mid-implementation** — initially shipped on `route-preview` per the original brief (right-overlay, info-blue), then moved to `route-planning` under the existing yellow hazard FAB (same accent colour, mutually exclusive — opening one cancels the other; `handleMapTap` and `handleMapLongPress` extended to suppress during suggestion mode; footer cascades through suggestion → hazard → normal). **Pre-existing bug uncovered + fixed:** dev APK from before `1a34b2e` (May 21 Google Sign-In commit) lacked `RNGoogleSignin` autolinking → `Invariant Violation: TurboModuleRegistry.getEnforcing(...)` escaped a try/catch wrapped only around `require()`, surfaced as a LogBox warning that read as a "stuck loading screen". Rebuilt the dev APK via `./gradlew installDevelopmentDebug` AND patched `signInWithGoogle` in `apps/mobile/src/lib/supabase.ts` to move the destructure INSIDE the try/catch — the access to `mod.GoogleSignin` is what triggers `getEnforcing`, not the `require()` itself. **Logged as error-log #45** with the broader rule (TurboModule destructure can escape the require's try/catch — pull the whole access into the same try). **Supabase dashboard gotcha worth noting:** RLS `SELECT auth.uid() = user_id` means the Table Editor (running as `authenticated`) shows zero rows even though `service_role` sees them — view via SQL Editor or set Table Editor role to `service_role`. **Verification:** `npm run typecheck` clean all three workspaces, `npm run check:bundle` HTTP 200, end-to-end live test recorded one row from a real user session. **Commits:** TBD.
- Session 56 (2026-05-21): **Daily weather notification — made it actually fire, then made the tap re-show it in-app. Four preview builds v0.2.57→v0.2.60.** Tester reported (a) no notification permission prompt, then (b) wanted the tap to re-show the message. **Root cause of the silent failure (the important learning, now in CLAUDE.md "Notifications" + error-log #21/#2b):** every notification guard checked `NativeModules.ExpoPushTokenManager`, which is `undefined` under the New Architecture (bridgeless) that the preview/production variants run — expo-notifications registers via the Expo Modules API, not the legacy RN bridge. So all notifications worked on the dev variant (old-arch bridge) and were silently dead on every release build. Two-step fix: **v0.2.58** added `ensureNotificationPermissionAsync()` (prompts once, respects `canAskAgain`) called from `DailyWeatherScheduler` before the location gate, since permission was previously only requested inside session-gated `registerForPushNotifications` — but this build still didn't prompt because the guard was the real problem. **v0.2.59** centralized detection in new `apps/mobile/src/lib/notificationNativeModule.ts` (`hasNotificationsNativeModule()` probing `requireOptionalNativeModule('ExpoPushTokenManager')` from `expo-modules-core`, arch-independent, legacy bridge fallback) and pointed all four consumers (`push-notifications.ts`, `daily-weather-notification.ts`, `NotificationProvider.tsx`, `DailyWeatherScheduler.tsx`) at it. Tester confirmed the prompt + the 8:30am ping. **Discovered while fixing:** `haptics.ts` carries the identical latent bug (`Boolean(NativeModules.ExpoHaptics)`) — flagged in CLAUDE.md, NOT yet fixed. **v0.2.60** — tap-to-reshow: scheduled notification now carries `data: { type: 'daily-weather', title, body, tone }` (tone via existing `isGoodCyclingWeather`); `handleNotificationResponse` stashes it in a transient (non-persisted) `weatherNotice` store field; new `WeatherNoticeManager` in `app/_layout.tsx` renders new `WeatherNoticeModal` molecule (Mascot `ride`/`rain` by tone), suppressed during NAVIGATING; works warm + cold start (existing `getLastNotificationResponseAsync` path). **Timing note (error-log #43):** tester saw the ping at 8:44 not 8:30 — expected Android Doze batching of `timeInterval` inexact alarms, NOT a bug. Left as-is by decision; rejected `SCHEDULE_EXACT_ALARM` (Play Store policy risk) and `DAILY` trigger (freezes content between app opens). **Verification:** typecheck + lint (0 regressions) + bundle HTTP 200 each build; 105 notification/store tests pass incl. new daily-weather tap test; added `expo-modules-core` mocks to two test files. All four APKs versionCode-bumped (59→62), audit-passed, distributed to Firebase `early-access-preview`. **Docs updated this session:** CLAUDE.md new "### Notifications" section + new-notification checklist, Key Decisions row + Gotcha #8 corrected, error-log #2b/#21 cross-referenced + #43 added. **Commits:** `600dd7c` (permission request), `f5fe7ad` (native-module detection fix), `ad9d9d8` (doc cross-refs), `748149e` (in-app tap modal), plus this doc commit. - Session 56 continued (2026-05-21): **v0.2.61 haptics fix + bridgeless Expo-guard sweep.** **v0.2.61 (versionCode 63, commit `ef79606`)** — fixed the latent haptics bug found during the notification work: `haptics.ts` AND `useHaptics.ts` both guarded on `Boolean(NativeModules.ExpoHaptics)`, so haptic feedback was silently dead on every preview/production (bridgeless) build, working only on the dev variant — identical root cause to the notification outage (error-log #21). Extracted the generic primitive `apps/mobile/src/lib/expoNativeModule.ts` → `hasExpoNativeModule(name)` (probes `requireOptionalNativeModule` from `expo-modules-core`, legacy-bridge fallback, try/catch for node); both haptics files now use `hasExpoNativeModule('ExpoHaptics')` and `notificationNativeModule.ts` was refactored to delegate to it — one canonical primitive for any Expo native-module presence check. Built, audit-passed, distributed to Firebase `early-access-preview`. **Then a full sweep** of every `NativeModules.X` guard in the app: **no other `NativeModules.Expo*` bugs remain.** Confirmed the Expo-vs-community distinction (now in error-log #21): Expo modules live in `globalThis.expo.modules` and are NEVER in `NativeModules`, but **community TurboModules (RNCNetInfo, RNViewShot) and core RN modules (I18nManager, SettingsManager) ARE exposed via the bridgeless interop proxy** — so their `NativeModules.<Name>` guards are correct and must NOT be "fixed" with `hasExpoNativeModule`. Verified each: `OffScreenCaptureHost` (RNViewShot) checks both NativeModules + `TurboModuleRegistry` (robust); `ConnectivityMonitor` (RNCNetInfo) matches how netinfo resolves itself on RN 0.83; `installReferrer` (PlayInstallReferrer) is a legacy bridge module so NativeModules is correct; `i18n` reads core modules with optional chaining + English fallback (minor: RO auto-detect could degrade to EN on some builds, not a crash — left as-is, manual locale override exists). Sweep produced no code changes. **All client-side fixes — Cloud Run API untouched all session.** Current tester build: **v0.2.61**. **Commits:** `ef79606` (haptics fix + generic helper) + this doc commit.
- Session 48 (2026-05-10): **Motion polish initiative — 4 phases shipped end-to-end as v0.2.45 → v0.2.46 → v0.2.47 → v0.2.48 preview builds, all distributed to Firebase `early-access-preview`.** Driven by user request to make the app "feel alive, in motion, premium" without breaking the safety contract. Decision tree: rejected `react-native-reanimated` install up front — Reanimated 4 needs New Architecture, dev variant has `newArchEnabled=false` (Windows Metro bridge constraint, see CLAUDE.md), Reanimated 3 may not support RN 0.83. Pivoted to react-native's built-in `Animated` API (already powering FadeSlideIn / Toggle / BadgeProgressBar / BottomSheet / Modal / particle overlays). Avoids APK rebuild, architecture flip, and bundle-size hit. Hard rules upheld every phase: every animation respects `useReducedMotion`; safety-critical surfaces (route line, hazard layers, GPS-quality dot) suppress motion when `appState === 'NAVIGATING'`; only `transform` + `opacity` JS-side, with Mapbox-native `*OpacityTransition` / `*RadiusTransition` for layer paint props; spring physics for response motions, timing for cross-fades; no new haptic intents. **P0 — everyday touchpoints** (commit `2776d7b`, 14 changed + 3 new): new `PressableScale` atom (the canonical press primitive: spring scale 0.96 + opacity + haptic intent prop, replaces ad-hoc `transform:[{scale:0.97}]` everywhere), `useStaggeredEntrance` hook (40ms-step cascade, mount-only, reduced-motion fallback), motion tokens extended (`springs.gentle/snappy/stiff/wobbly`, `EXIT_RATIO=0.7`, stagger constants); Button + Card switched to `PressableScale`-backed press; TextInput focus border colour crossfades over 150ms (border width still snaps 1→2 to avoid layout reflow); BottomNav got a single sliding accent indicator at the top of the bar (translateX between tab centers via stiff spring) plus an icon scale-pop on inactive→active transition; CategoryTabBar pills cross-fade per-pill bg/text from resting to category accent; new `ModeTogglePill` component (extracted from route-planning's inline 3 Pressables, kept in `src/components/` since the variant→colour mapping is coupled to routing UX) drives the Safe/Fast/Flat selector with the same crossfade pattern; LikeButton/LoveButton bloom (1 → 1.35 → 1, wobbly→snappy spring) on tap; Stack screen transitions configured at root for directional slide (`slide_from_right` forward, fade fallback under reduced motion). Released as **v0.2.45 (versionCode 47, commit `2ddea4c`)**. **P1 — screen rhythm** (commit `516d995`, 8 changed): list stagger via existing `FadeSlideIn` (`history.tsx` + `community-feed.tsx` already had it; added to `trips.tsx`, `achievements.tsx`, `my-shares.tsx`, `blocked-users.tsx` with delay = `Math.min(index, stagger.maxItems) * stagger.step` so the cascade tail stays under ~480ms even on long lists); Modal backdrop animates `rgba(0,0,0,0)` → `rgba(0,0,0,0.6)` over 150ms instead of snapping (restructured overlay so an animated outer `Animated.View` carries the bg colour and an inner `StyleSheet.absoluteFill` Pressable handles tap-to-dismiss; card sits on top); BottomSheet organism + MapStageScreen's CollapsibleSheet drag handle does a one-shot opacity pulse 800ms after first mount (1.0 ↔ 0.5 over 350ms each phase, two cycles, gated by `hasPulsedRef` so visibility toggles don't replay it). Released as **v0.2.46 (versionCode 48, commit `87aa11f`)**. **P2 — map surface** (commit `64da791`, 4 changed): NavigationHUD's GPS-quality dot crossfades backgroundColor between the 4 tiers (gray→red→amber→green) over 200ms via Animated.Value tier-index interpolation (the existing `PulsingGpsIcon` "poor signal" loop is left untouched); `RouteLayers` ramps `lineOpacity` 0→target via Mapbox native `lineOpacityTransition: { duration: 500 }` on first paint of a non-empty route, with `hasAnimatedRef` gating against replay on alternative-selection / reroute; `HazardLayers` (zones, cluster bubbles, individual markers, labels) ramps opacity 0→target via `circleOpacityTransition` / `lineOpacityTransition` / `textOpacityTransition` on first paint, **suppressed during NAVIGATING** (riders need hazards visible instantly, never with a 500ms delay); 4 floating action buttons in route-planning (recenter, hazard-mode toggle, nearby places, saved routes) switched from plain `Pressable` to `PressableScale` for consistent spring-press feedback. **OverpassPoiLayers fade-in deferred** — its conditional-render + `key`-prop force-remount pattern would have needed more refactoring than P2 warranted; bicycle parking/rental/shop markers still appear instantly. Recenter camera animation itself was already 600ms `easeTo` via `Mapbox.Camera animationDuration` — left untouched (the `recenterKey`-in-`key` force-remount is a known minor wart, not worth a refactor without device testing). **Confirmed `lineOpacityTransition` / `circleOpacityTransition` are typed first-class props in `@rnmapbox/maps@10.1.41`** by grep on `node_modules/@rnmapbox/maps/lib/typescript/src/utils/MapboxStyles.d.ts` before relying on them. Released as **v0.2.47 (versionCode 49, commit `680f494`)**. **P3 — celebration & delight** (commit `4e56ab4`, 8 changed + 1 new): new `IdlePulse` atom (loops opacity 1.0 ↔ 0.55 over 1.1s phases, sparingly used for empty states); StreakCard's flame icon does a gentle scale + opacity flicker (0.96↔1.04, 0.85↔1.0 over 800ms each phase) when `currentStreak >= 3` (extracted inline `FlickerFlame` helper); Toast's `success` variant gets an additional spring scale-bounce (0.92 → 1.04 → 1, wobbly→snappy) layered onto the existing slide+fade entrance — info/warning/error stay firm; `MarkerLayers` destination CircleLayer (outer red ring + inner white dot bullseye) animates `circleRadius` 0× → 1.25× → 1.0× over 400ms via `circleRadiusTransition` when a NEW destination coordinate appears (lastDestKeyRef gates against replay on map re-renders), suppressed during NAVIGATING and reduced motion; empty-state icons on `history.tsx` (bicycle-outline) and `blocked-users.tsx` (happy-outline) wrapped in `IdlePulse` (community-feed and trips empty states are text-only and were left alone); TierRankCard XP progress bar gets a 24px-wide white shine sweep (translateX -24 → fillEnd over 700ms with opacity 0→1→0) when `totalXp` grows between renders. **Particle drift was considered for the XP bar** but the 6px-tall track has `overflow:'hidden'` and its parent `rightCol` has flexible layout — particles would have needed to be siblings of the track positioned absolutely, requiring layout refactor; the shine sweep delivers the same "energy flowing" read with no layout change. **Onboarding mascot bob dropped from P3** — the audit confirmed goal-selection.tsx, safety-score.tsx, and other onboarding screens use plain icons (briefcase, compass, bicycle) rather than character mascots; nothing to bob. - Session 47 continued (2026-05-10): **v0.2.43 Mia retirement preview shipped + v0.2.44 Play Store URL in all share text.** v0.2.43 (versionCode 45, commit `fdc7791`) cut and distributed to Firebase `early-access-preview`. Tester confirmed full destination search, all routing modes, and full route-preview UI now available regardless of onboarding path; Confident Cyclist badge unlocks on first ride; profile referral row clean (no `?persona=mia`). **v0.2.44 (versionCode 46, commit `314fc24`):** added `PLAY_STORE_URL = 'https://play.google.com/store/apps/details?id=com.defensivepedal.mobile&pcampaignid=web_share'` constant to `packages/core/src/shareCaption.ts` (`pcampaignid=web_share` lights up Google's Share install attribution in Play Console). Six share surfaces updated: (1) profile "Help a friend" referral row — replaced the in-app `Linking.createURL('/')` deep-link (a `defensivepedal-preview://` scheme useless to non-installers) with the public Play Store URL; (2) `buildShareCaption` (ride/milestone/badge) — Play Store URL appended after hashtags, covers `useShareRide` + `useShareCard` automatically; (3) `useShareRoute` planned + saved route share — `Get Defensive Pedal: <url>` line below the route share webUrl; (4) `my-shares.tsx` re-share — same suffix; (5) `route-planning.tsx` hazard-alert share — appended to message; (6) `MilestoneShareCard.getMilestoneShareText` — appended (currently unreferenced but kept consistent). Tested live: 502 core tests pass with new assertion; tester confirmed Profile referral, route share, and hazard alert all show the URL. **Known gap (accepted, not fixed):** badge/milestone/ride image shares (the captures rendered to PNG via `OffScreenCaptureHost` and shared via `lib/shareImage.ts` → `expo-sharing`'s `Sharing.shareAsync`) do NOT carry the URL to recipients. Root cause: `Sharing.shareAsync(fileUri, { mimeType, dialogTitle })` only takes a file URI and a dialog title; there's no body-text field, so the `caption` parameter we pass becomes the share-sheet header (visible only to the sharer) and never propagates to the receiving app. The image itself carries the brand visually (Defensive Pedal logo + stats baked in by the share card), so the gap is acceptable for these surfaces. Future fix would require either burning the URL into the image at capture time (small QR + footer text on the share card) or routing image shares through React Native's `Share.share()` API instead of `expo-sharing` — but `Share.share`'s `url` field doesn't reliably accept `file://` paths on Android. **Commits this continuation:** `fdc7791` (release bump 0.2.43), `39937cf` (docs session 47 part 1), `314fc24` (Play Store URL share + bump 0.2.44). Backend unchanged: still on Cloud Run revision `defpedal-api-00077-xj7`.
- Session 46 (2026-05-08): **v0.2.38 — onboarding Skip button + Goal-screen freeze fix; preview rebuild distributed; production AAB cut for Play Console.** Two changes shipped on top of Session 45's Play Store readiness work: (1) **Skip button across the onboarding flow** — new shared hook `apps/mobile/src/hooks/useSkipOnboarding.ts` mirrors `signup-prompt`'s `finishOnboarding` (sets `onboardingCompleted=true`, captures analytics opt-out as default if user hadn't reached the consent step yet, conditional `resetAnonymousOpenCount` only on initial completion so count-based re-prompts don't loop, drops the demo route via `resetFlow()`, `router.replace('/route-planning')`). Top-right Skip pill rendered on `/onboarding/index` (separate from existing "Skip for now" footer link that only advances one step), `/onboarding/consent`, `/onboarding/safety-score` (floating above the map), `/onboarding/goal-selection` (paired with chevron-back in a header row), `/onboarding/first-route` (same pattern). `signup-prompt.tsx` left alone — its existing "Maybe later" already exits the flow and is intentionally hidden when `mandatory=true`. (2) **Goal-screen freeze bug fix** — tester reported pressing system back returned to a Goal screen where every goal card was unresponsive. Diagnosis: Goal advances to `/onboarding/first-route` via `router.push`, so on first-route the stack is `[index, consent, goal-selection, first-route]` — Goal is preserved underneath, NOT unmounted. When the user picks a goal, `hasNavigatedRef.current = true` locks against double-firing. System back from first-route re-focuses the same instance with the ref still `true`, so `handleSelect` and `handleDismiss` short-circuit on every press, with no state update to trigger a re-render — looks like a hard freeze. Fix: `useFocusEffect(useCallback(() => { hasNavigatedRef.current = false; }, []))` re-arms the ref on every focus. Same defensive reset added to `safety-score.tsx` even though forward nav from there uses `router.replace` (removes it from stack) — belt-and-suspenders. **Phone-test detour worth recording:** `adb reverse` was consistently 8s+ per HTTP request on this Windows host (raw `adb shell` was fast at 78 ms; `adb shell dd if=/dev/zero bs=1M count=4 | wc -c` ran in 117 ms = ~34 MB/s, so the USB pipe itself is healthy — the adb reverse pipe specifically is broken). Fresh `kill-server`/`start-server` cycle didn't help; switching to `adb tcpip 5555` over WiFi was even worse (all timeouts). Symptom on device: `loadJSBundleFromMetro()` hangs forever, dev app sits at blank Splash. Root cause likely Windows Defender or AV interfering with adb's TCP forwarding (raw transport packets clean, port-forward connections not). Workaround: skipped the dev variant entirely and went straight to preview build (embedded bundle, no Metro dependency). Two failed dev-build attempts before that — first crashed the JVM with multi-ABI CMake OOM (`-Xmx4096m` × parallel daemons + Kotlin daemon overflowed Windows commit limit), second hit error 1455 "paging file too small" — eventually succeeded with `--no-daemon --max-workers=1 -PreactNativeArchitectures=arm64-v8a -Dorg.gradle.jvmargs="-Xmx3072m -XX:MaxMetaspaceSize=768m"` (3m total). The dev APK was actually built and `adb install`ed, but Metro could never serve the bundle because of the broken reverse, so the dev app is unusable in this env until adb reverse is fixed (replace USB cable; check Defender/AV exclusions; or temporarily disable real-time protection). **Preview distributed:** `npm run build:preview` (4m, audit clean), AAB-equivalent APK 177 MB, upload-keystore signed `82:7C:FD:…:35:73`, pushed to Firebase App Distribution group `early-access-preview` via app `1:1070156882676:android:e8942c210dc337ebca34a1` ("Defensive Pedal Preview"). - Session 44 (2026-05-06): **Route-preview bottom-sheet swipe-up reliability fix.** Tester reported swipe-up on the collapsed sheet at `/route-preview` worked intermittently and required multiple attempts; swipe-down was fine. Root cause in `apps/mobile/src/components/MapStageScreen.tsx`'s `CollapsibleSheet`: the `PanResponder` was attached to a `<View>` wrapping only the 48px drag handle (the inner `Pressable` for tap-to-toggle). The `peekContent` row (60px tall — the strip with "Safe · 2.9 km · 15 min" + "Swipe up" hint) was rendered as a **sibling** of that view with no touch handlers. So when collapsed (≈108px visible: handle + peek), only swipes that happened to start on the narrow handle bar registered — and those still had to fight the inner Pressable's responder claim until 8px of vertical drag triggered the move-capture. Swipe-down felt fine because when expanded, the handle is the obvious top edge to swipe from with nothing competing for visual attention. Fix: moved the peek row **inside** the pan-responder wrapper. Now touches on the peek strip have no descendant claiming the responder, so the parent's `onStartShouldSetPanResponder: () => true` grabs immediately and `onPanResponderMove` fires from the first frame. Touches on the handle still go through the existing flow (Pressable claims → move-capture takes over after 8px → swipe works) so tap-to-toggle is preserved. When expanded, the peek row isn't rendered, so the panResponder area shrinks to just the handle — same as before, no interference with content scrolling. **Verification:** typecheck clean across api + mobile + web. Bundle check HTTP 200. Built `installDevelopmentDebug` (3m 28s, BUILD SUCCESSFUL); on the SM-S918B test device, the first launch hit the known dev-build blank-screen pitfall — ADB reverse 8081/8080 were set *after* the app process started, so the bundle download hung at `loadJSBundleFromMetro()`. `adb shell am force-stop com.defensivepedal.mobile.dev` + relaunch fixed it (bundle loaded in <2s, `Running "main" with fabric:true`). Tester confirmed the swipe-up fix: works smoothly from anywhere on the collapsed strip now. Tap-to-toggle on the handle still works. Swipe-down on the expanded sheet unchanged. **Side observation (not actioned):** runtime logs show `fabric:true` on the dev variant, contradicting CLAUDE.md's "development = bridge mode (newArchEnabled=false)" docs. `gradle.properties` has `newArchEnabled=false` but `BuildConfig.IS_NEW_ARCHITECTURE_ENABLED` came out `true` — Expo SDK 55's `ExpoReactHostFactory.getDefaultReactHost()` appears to force bridgeless on RN 0.83 regardless of the project property. `@rnmapbox/maps` 10.1.41 view managers throw soft `getDelegate` exceptions in fabric mode (RNMBXCamera, RNMBXShapeSource, RNMBXLineLayer, etc.) but none are fatal — the map still renders via the legacy view path. This has been in place since at least session 43 (when v0.2.31 shipped working). Worth aligning the doc to runtime reality next time CLAUDE.md gets a touch-up. **Commit:** single-file change to `MapStageScreen.tsx`. No version bump (mobile-only, dev-build verified, no app distribution this session).

Ship plan executed end-to-end. **Implementation:** (1) `apps/mobile/app.config.ts` — `orientation: 'portrait'` → `'default'`; `apps/mobile/android/app/src/main/AndroidManifest.xml` — dropped `android:screenOrientation="portrait"` from MainActivity (Expo prebuild regenerates from app.config so direct manifest edit is current-state cleanup, not tracked). (2) New `expo-screen-orientation ~55.0.14` installed in `apps/mobile/package.json` (NOT root — autolinker only reads workspace per error #22). (3) New `apps/mobile/src/hooks/useLockOrientation.ts` — wraps `lockAsync(PORTRAIT_UP)` in `useFocusEffect` from expo-router so the lock is tied to FOCUS, not mount/unmount. **Critical because `expo-screen-orientation`'s lock is process-level (applies to whole activity), and Expo Router's stack keeps screens mounted underneath pushed routes** — `useEffect` cleanup wouldn't fire when navigating to a new screen, leaving the entire app locked. First implementation used `NativeModules.ExpoScreenOrientation` as a guard which always returned false because Expo modules register through `expo-modules-core`, not the legacy RN bridge `NativeModules` registry (project error-prevention rule #21) — guard removed, replaced with try/catch around `require()`. Native module name confirmed `ExpoScreenOrientation` in `node_modules/expo-screen-orientation/android/.../ScreenOrientationModule.kt`. (4) `useLockOrientation()` called from `route-planning.tsx:84`, `route-preview.tsx:81`, `navigation.tsx:112`. (5) **Trophy Case (`achievements.tsx`) responsive grid** — `useWindowDimensions` drives a 3-column (portrait) → 5-column (≥600dp / landscape) grid via `LANDSCAPE_BREAKPOINT_DP=600`. `FlatList key={\`grid-${numColumns}\`}` forces remount on column-count change since RN rejects mid-life `numColumns` updates. `cellWidth` recomputed reactively, added to `renderItem` `useCallback` deps. (6) **Modal/overlay particle containers** (`BadgeUnlockOverlay.tsx`, `MiaLevelUpOverlay.tsx`) replaced explicit `width: SCREEN_W, height: SCREEN_H` with `...StyleSheet.absoluteFillObject` — fills parent regardless of orientation. `MiaLevelUpOverlay`'s testimonial wrap moved from `width: SCREEN_W - space[8] * 2` to `alignSelf: 'stretch'` + `marginHorizontal: space[8]` so it reflows on rotation. (7) `PoiCard.tsx` migrated to `useWindowDimensions` for consistency (still on portrait-locked screens — future-proof only). (8) `MiaInvitationPrompt.tsx` had a dead `SCREEN_H` import — removed. (9) **Dimensions.get migrations skipped** — `SearchBar.tsx` (only on portrait-locked /route-planning), `MapStageScreen.tsx:22` (only consumed by portrait-locked screens), share-card components (snapshot images, displayed once), `BottomSheet.tsx` (already reactive via `Dimensions.addEventListener('change')`). **supabase-js refresh-token cosmetic noise silenced.** Tester reported "AuthApiError: Invalid Refresh Token" on cold-start dev install (recurring). The library logs `console.error('AuthApiError: Invalid Refresh Token: Refresh Token not found')` whenever `getSession()` encounters an expired refresh token, but it still gracefully returns `{ session: null }` — `AuthSessionProvider` falls through to anonymous sign-in correctly. The error is purely cosmetic but triggers RN's LogBox overlay in dev and spams Sentry in prod. Fix: `apps/mobile/src/lib/supabase.ts` installs a narrow `console.error` filter at module load that drops two specific messages (`'Invalid Refresh Token: Refresh Token not found'` + `'Invalid Refresh Token: Already Used'`); everything else passed through unchanged. **Verification flow during implementation:** First lock implementation used `useEffect` + `NativeModules` guard — tester reported "screen rotates during navigation as well" because the broken guard meant lock never fired anywhere; fixed `NativeModules` issue, retested → tester reported "now no screen rotates, all are fixed in portrait" — discovered the process-level-lock + push-not-replace stack interaction. Switched `useEffect` → `useFocusEffect`, third test confirmed the right behavior: rotatable on Profile/History/Community, locked on /route-planning, /route-preview, /navigation. **Commit `11b91a6`** ("feat(mobile): auto-rotate non-map screens (Tier 1 landscape support)") — 13 files, +128/-27. - Session 42 (2026-05-05): **v0.2.30 — UX cleanup sweep across destination gating, weather warning, and onboarding/sign-in flow.** Six tester-driven fixes shipped in commit `00f996f`. **(1) Preview Route is now disabled when no destination is set** — `route-planning.tsx:1257-1278` adds `disabled={!hasValidDestination}` to the primary CTA and renders an inline helper "Enter a destination to continue" beneath. New `planning.enterDestinationFirst` i18n key (EN + RO). Bug was that the button was tappable on `(0,0)` coords, leading to nonsense routes. **(2) Map long-press tooltip wording** — "Long-press map to drop a pin" → "Longpress to set as destination" (`route-planning.tsx:798`). **(3) WeatherWarningModal stops appearing on top of /profile after sign-out** — `route-preview.tsx:469` now reads `useIsFocused()` from `expo-router` and gates `visible` on it. Bug mechanism: the modal renders into a separate native window above the entire app, so even when route-preview is sitting under /profile in the stack, RN's Modal still pops on top. After sign-out, `UserCacheResetBridge` runs `queryClient.clear()` on the user-id transition, forcing `useWeather` to refetch and re-evaluate the modal's `visible` prop without `weatherWarningDismissed` blocking it. The `useIsFocused` gate hides the modal whenever route-preview isn't the active screen. **(4) Temperature swing warning now matches the day's actual trend** — previously every swing warning said "layer up" regardless of direction, even on a warming-up day. Two-part fix: (a) added `remainingTempTrend: 'rising' | 'falling' | 'mixed'` to `WeatherData` (`weather.ts:32-46`); (b) computed in `fetchWeather` from the **first vs last** remaining-day hour with a 3°C threshold (`weather.ts:236-251`) — robust to non-monotonic evening forecasts that fooled the prior argmin/argmax-position logic (e.g., `[18, 22, 20, 18, 16]` was incorrectly classified as 'rising' because the absolute min landed at the END of the window while the start was tied with a mid value). End-vs-start ignores transient bumps and reads the rider's actual experience. Three message branches: rising → "Warming up later today, start in light layers and pack water"; falling → "Cooling down later today, pack a layer"; mixed → neutral "Big temperature swing, dress in layers". 6 new unit tests in `weather.test.ts` (3 for trend computation in `fetchWeather` using `vi.setSystemTime`, 3 for trend-specific message branching in `getWeatherWarnings`) — all 39 tests green. **(5) Sign-out no longer routes the user into onboarding** — `UserCacheResetBridge.tsx:40-78` adds an effect that flips `onboardingCompleted=true` whenever the user holds a real (non-anonymous) account, regardless of how they got there (/auth direct, signup-prompt, OAuth callback). Previously only `signup-prompt.tsx` set the flag, so users who signed in via the Profile "Sign in" CTA → /auth would have `onboardingCompleted=false`, and a subsequent sign-out + anonymous-sign-in cycle would hit the `computeOnboardingGateTarget` branch that sends `onboardingCompleted === false` users to `/onboarding`. The bridge centralizes the rule. **(6) Sign-in (or finishing onboarding) no longer auto-routes the user into /route-preview** — `signup-prompt.tsx:73-75` (`finishOnboarding`) and `signup-prompt.tsx:104-110` (`handleGoogleSignIn`) used to redirect to `/route-preview` if a persisted route preview existed (the demo circuit route generated by `/onboarding/first-route.tsx:196`). Now both always `router.replace('/route-planning')` and call `resetFlow()` to drop the demo circuit route from Zustand. Same change applied to `choose-username.tsx:46-49` (existing-username early-return) and `:87-91` (`navigateToApp`). Stale comment about `routePreview` capture removed. **All workspaces typecheck clean. - Session 41 (2026-05-05): **v0.2.29 — History screen now refetches on focus.** After session 40's DB-migration fix unblocked trip recording, tester reported "tapped retry dead mutations, no new trips visible. New trip with zero movement saved, doesn't appear in My Trips". Confirmed via direct SQL on Supabase: 3 fresh `trip_tracks` rows for user `dd2494f1-…` (one zero-movement trip + two recovered orphans). Cloud Run logs confirmed `/v1/trips/start`, `/v1/trips/end`, `/v1/trips/track`, and `/v1/trips/history` all returned 200. Data was in DB and the endpoint returned it — but the History screen wasn't showing it. Root cause: `apps/mobile/app/trips.tsx` had `staleTime: 60_000` on the `['trip-history']` React Query and no refetch-on-focus. Tabs in this app stay mounted across switches (BottomNav uses `router.replace` but the underlying screens don't fully unmount/remount the way default Stack screens do for the `refetchOnMount` heuristic to fire correctly), so trips that synced AFTER the user last looked at History stayed invisible behind the cache for up to 60 seconds. Fix: imported `useFocusEffect` from expo-router and call `refetch()` on every focus. Lowered `staleTime` from 60s → 10s as a backstop. Switching to Profile and back, or returning from /feedback, immediately surfaces the latest trips. Recovery path for tester's orphaned trips also works without an install — force-quit + reopen bypasses the cache and shows the trips. **v0.2.29 distributed:** versionName `0.2.28` → `0.2.29`, versionCode `30` → `31`. - Session 40 (2026-05-05): **Critical hotfix — `/v1/trips/start` has been 502'ing since session 33 (2026-04-27); zero trips recorded for 8 days.** Tester reported "no trips recorded — neither user-stopped nor app-killed". Cloud Run logs confirmed every `/v1/trips/start` POST since 2026-04-27 returned 502 with `outcome: server_error`, retried by the offline queue every 15s, then cascade-killed trip_end + trip_track after MAX_RETRY_COUNT. Root cause: migration `202604270002_trip_idempotency.sql` (session 33) created a **partial** unique index `trips_user_client_trip_id_unique` with `WHERE (client_trip_id IS NOT NULL)`. The route handler (`startTripRecord` in `services/mobile-api/src/lib/submissions.ts`) uses Supabase's `.upsert(rows, { onConflict: 'user_id,client_trip_id' })`, which PostgREST translates to bare `ON CONFLICT (user_id, client_trip_id) DO UPDATE`. PostgreSQL rejects this with `42P10: there is no unique or exclusion constraint matching the ON CONFLICT specification` because partial unique indexes require the explicit `WHERE` in the conflict target — and PostgREST's `onConflict` parameter only accepts a column list, no WHERE clause. The bug was masked by the deploy smoke-test only hitting `/health`; nobody ran an end-to-end trip after the partial index landed. **Fix:** new migration `202605050001_trip_idempotency_drop_partial_where.sql` drops and recreates the index without the WHERE clause. NULL client_trip_id rows remain valid (PostgreSQL treats NULL as DISTINCT in unique indexes by default), so legacy data is unaffected and the semantic of the index — "uniqueness on (user_id, client_trip_id) when client_trip_id is set" — is preserved. Verified via raw SQL: the upsert pattern now passes the conflict-resolution check (FK error remains for fake user, but that's expected). Migration applied via Supabase MCP. **No Cloud Run redeploy needed** — the bug is purely server-side DB schema; the route code is correct. **Tester recovery path:** open Diagnostics → tap "Retry dead mutations". Orphaned trip_start mutations from the past 8 days will retry, succeed, set the tripId mapping, and the previously-cascade-killed trip_end / trip_track will sync — orphaned trips will finally appear in History. New rides going forward work normally. Cloud Run revision unchanged at `defpedal-api-00073-ftt`. **Behavioural note for future migrations:** when adding a partial unique index intended to be used as an ON CONFLICT target via PostgREST's onConflict parameter, the index must NOT be partial — PostgREST cannot emit the WHERE clause. Either keep the index non-partial (NULL handling preserves semantics) or use a raw RPC for the upsert.
- Session 39 (2026-05-05): **v0.2.28 hotfix — Light/System theme actually applies now.** Tester reported "no screens flip to light" when picking Light or System in Profile → Display. Code audit confirmed `themePreference` is correctly persisted, all screens use `useTheme()` + `createThemedStyles(colors)`, and Zustand wiring is intact — but the force-dark gate at the top of `ThemeContext.tsx` was firing whenever `appState === 'NAVIGATING' || appState === 'ROUTE_PREVIEW'`. Since `appState` persists across screen transitions (the user stays in `ROUTE_PREVIEW` after backing out of route-preview to bottom-nav into Profile), the force-dark made the theme picker **silently inert on every non-map screen** until the user cleared appState back to `IDLE` (e.g., by completing a ride or hitting reset). The bug had been there since the P1-30 design pass (commit `7b678ee`); not a regression from any of my recent work, but my test-plan for the bug-fix sweep specifically prompted it. Fix: gate force-dark on the actual `usePathname()` from `expo-router` — `MAP_STAGE_PATHS = new Set(['/route-preview', '/navigation'])` — so the rule only fires when the user is truly viewing a map-stage screen on a (likely) handlebar mount. Profile, History, Community, onboarding, settings, and route-planning all respect `themePreference` regardless of background appState. **v0.2.28 distributed:** versionName `0.2.27` → `0.2.28`, versionCode `29` → `30`. Build via `npm run build:preview` (audit clean, upload-keystore signed `82:7C:FD:…:35:73`, 186 MB). Pushed to Firebase App Distribution group `early-access-preview`. Tester link: `https://appdistribution.firebase.google.com/testerapps/1:1070156882676:android:e8942c210dc337ebca34a1/releases/0fjlbhg3qllk0`. Backend stays on Cloud Run revision `defpedal-api-00073-ftt`.
- Session 38 (2026-05-04): **v0.2.27 hotfix — revert Phase 5 auth mutex + harden screen-keep-awake during navigation.** Tester reported v0.2.26 was *deterministically* dropping the Google sign-in on every cold start and routing to onboarding. Root cause: my Phase 5 mutex in `apps/mobile/src/providers/AuthSessionProvider.tsx` (commit `0be37e2`) — `pendingRerun` made the post-mount sync run *deterministically* after the mount sync rather than racing it. When Supabase's cold-start refresh-and-emit sequence produced a `SIGNED_OUT` (e.g., transient refresh hiccup), the rerun's `getCurrentSession()` ran late enough that Supabase's internal store had already been cleared, returned `null`, and the rerun called `setSession(null)` with `allowAnonSignIn=false` — wiping the real session and tripping `_layout.tsx`'s OnboardingGuard imperative redirect. The pre-Phase-5 code's race-condition setSession ordering was actually masking this: in OLD code, the original mount sync's `setSession(realSession)` call could land *after* the listener's `setSession(null)`, "accidentally" preserving the session. My deterministic ordering exposed the underlying issue. Reverted just the mutex (`AuthSessionProvider.tsx` back to pre-`0be37e2` state); Phases 1-4 stay live and unchanged. The original P1 finding (rare logged-out flash) is back open as a known cosmetic issue — needs a different fix, probably "don't `setSession(null)` from rerun if mount sync already set a non-null session in this lifecycle". **Screen-keep-awake hardening:** tester also reported the phone screen dims and goes dark during navigation. `useKeepAwake()` had been there since long before my changes, so this isn't a regression — but the hook's silent-failure mode meant we couldn't tell whether the native module was actually binding. Replaced `useKeepAwake()` with explicit `activateKeepAwakeAsync('defensivepedal-navigation')` + `deactivateKeepAwake` in a `useEffect`, with `console.warn` on activation failure (same defensive pattern as error-log #21/#23). If the native module ever fails to bind on a future build, the dev overlay will surface it instead of silently letting the screen sleep. Stable per-screen tag dedupes overlapping activations. **v0.2.27 distributed:** versionName `0.2.26` → `0.2.27`, versionCode `28` → `29`. - Session 37 (2026-05-04): **/review bug-fix sweep — 14 P1 defects shipped across 5 phases.** Multi-agent code review of the working tree surfaced 14 real-impact correctness bugs (no P0s); fixed all of them in five sequenced batches. Report saved at `review-report-2026-05-04.md`. **Phase 1 — offline mutation queue (5 fixes):** `polylineSegmentDistance` now bounds-guards `fromIndex >= points.length - 1` instead of returning a coincidentally-correct 0 (`packages/core/src/distance.ts:30-44` + 2 regression tests); `OfflineMutationSyncManager` re-reads `useAppStore.getState()` after `markMutationSyncing` and after each `await` so post-await `setTripServerId`/`resolveMutation` operate on fresh `tripServerIds` instead of a pre-await snapshot; `NavigationLifecycleManager.tsx:43` reads `state.routeRequest?.mode` instead of hardcoding `'fast'` on app-kill recovery (every kill-recovered safe ride was being mis-labeled in `trip_tracks.routing_mode`); `navigation.tsx:347-371` `queueTripEnd` now reads `store.queuedMutations.some(...)` from the live store instead of a closure-captured `hasQueuedTripEnd`, so two callers in the same render tick (auto-completion effect + unmount cleanup) both see the first enqueue and bail; `queueSlice.ts:254-273` documents `killMutation`'s idempotency contract + new test locks it in (cascade-kill loop in OfflineMutationSyncManager depends on it). **Phase 2 — navigation completion (3 fixes):** `navigation.ts:421-455` adds an independent destination-distance gate to `shouldCompleteNavigation` — completion now requires `arrivedAtManeuver && onLastStep && (haversine(user, lastVertex) <= ARRIVAL_THRESHOLD + gpsAccuracy)`. Without this, a closestPointIndex snap past the penultimate maneuver advanced currentStepIndex to the arrival waypoint and zeroed distanceToManeuver, completing the ride while the rider was still meters away. Also surfaces real haversine remaining on the FooterCard when polyline-projection is 0 but rider isn't at destination. `appStore.ts:657-678` `finishNavigation` is now idempotent: it reconciles `appState=AWAITING_FEEDBACK` even when the session is already in `awaiting_feedback` (covers rehydration drift) and is a strict no-op for `idle`/`preview`. `appStore.ts:586-608` + `route-preview.tsx:365-376` add a same-route double-tap re-entry guard on `startNavigation` (preserves the live session's breadcrumbs + step index) and an early-return on `beginNavigation` (prevents duplicate `trip_start` enqueue with a fresh `clientTripId` — server-side idempotency keys on `(user_id, client_trip_id)` so distinct ids = distinct trips). New regression test confirms 40m perpendicular off-route doesn't complete prematurely. **Phase 3 — auth tier corrections (3 fixes):** new `requireFullUser` helper in `feed-helpers.ts`; all four follow write endpoints (`POST/DELETE /users/:id/follow`, `POST .../approve`, `POST .../decline`) swapped from `requireUser` → `requireFullUser` so anonymous Supabase sessions get 403 instead of polluting target users' follower lists / activity feeds. New dedicated `leaderboard` rate-limit bucket (30/min default, env-overridable) so heavy tab-switching on City Heartbeat no longer starves a rider's actual route-preview budget. Removed phantom `clientTripId` from `/trips/history` response schema (the column wasn't in the SELECT, the contract type didn't expose it, and no client read it). **Phase 4 — hazard scaling (2 fixes):** `/hazards/:id/validate` now uses the dedicated `hazardVote` 5-per-10-min bucket instead of the global `write` bucket (writes to the same `hazard_validations` table as `/vote` — the legacy endpoint was a vote-throttle bypass). New PostGIS RPC `get_nearby_hazards(p_user_lat, p_user_lon, p_radius_meters, p_limit=200)` (migration `202605040001_get_nearby_hazards.sql`) replaces the JS-side degree-bbox + 200-row truncation pattern in `/v1/hazards/nearby`. `ST_DWithin` against geography-cast JSONB lat/lon, `is_hidden`/`expires_at`/`score>-3` gates moved server-side. The LIMIT now lands AFTER the radius filter — what the API actually wanted. Previous code silently dropped older hazards inside the radius once any city had >200 active hazards and drifted at high latitudes (1° lon ≠ 111km away from equator). **Phase 5 — auth flicker (1 fix):** `AuthSessionProvider.tsx:50-127` adds `syncInFlight` mutex + `pendingRerun` flag inside the auth `useEffect`. Concurrent `syncCurrentSession` calls (mount sync racing `onAuthStateChange` listeners during anonymous sign-in) are now serialized: the second caller doesn't fire its own `setSession(null)` mid-flight; if a state change arrived during the window, exactly one follow-up sync runs after the current finishes — no dropped transitions, no logged-out flash. **Migration applied:** `get_nearby_hazards` via Supabase MCP. **Cloud Run revision:** `defpedal-api-00073-ftt` serving 100% traffic, build digest `sha256:5786d89c...`, `/health` 200, `/v1/hazards/nearby` 200 with empty array (consistent with 0 active hazards in DB). **Tests:** ~155 affected tests across core + mobile + api, all green. - Session 34 (2026-04-28): **P1.1 follow-up — trip delete now scrubs community surfaces too.** Diagnosis flagged that the just-shipped `DELETE /v1/trips/:id` only removed the `trip_tracks` row, leaving the auto-shared `trip_shares` row and the unified `activity_feed` `'ride'` entry behind. Result: a deleted trip vanished from History + Stats but lingered in City Heartbeat aggregates, Community Stats, the Neighborhood Leaderboard's `trip_shares`-based ride counts, the Community Feed card, and the social Activity Feed (incl. follower feeds). All four community surfaces read from `trip_shares` (`get_city_heartbeat`, `get_community_stats`, `get_neighborhood_leaderboard`, `get_nearby_feed`) or `activity_feed` (`get_ranked_feed`), never from `trip_tracks` — so a trip-tracks-only delete created a real divergence. Fix: `deleteTripTrack` now does three sequential cleanups in a single handler — `(a)` `DELETE FROM trip_tracks ... .select('id, trip_id')` to capture the parent `trip_id` atomically, `(b)` `DELETE FROM trip_shares WHERE user_id = ? AND trip_id = parent_trip_id` (cascades to `feed_likes` / `feed_comments` / `trip_loves` via existing FK rules), `(c)` `DELETE FROM activity_feed WHERE user_id = ? AND type = 'ride' AND payload->>tripId = parent_trip_id` (cascades to `activity_reactions` / `activity_comments`). All three deletes are user-scoped as defence-in-depth; `(b)` and `(c)` are skipped when the deleted track had a NULL `trip_id` (legacy data). `not_found` short-circuits before touching downstream tables. Confirm copy updated in EN + RO: "removed from your history **and from the community feed**" so users know what to expect. Tests rebuilt: 7 cases now (success path verifies all three table deletes + their scope filters, not_found / null_data / db_error short-circuit, share-cleanup error → 502 surface, activity-cleanup error → 502 surface, NULL-trip_id legacy path skips downstream). Mobile-api submissions tests 16/16 + v1 routes 25/25 green. Pre-existing failure in `routes-feed.test.ts > POST /v1/feed/:id/comments` (2 cases, returns 500 instead of 200/502) confirmed present on `main` `8c224ce` before my edits — out of scope for this slice. Repo-wide typecheck + bundle check green. **Note: leaderboard_snapshots intentionally NOT touched** — those are immutable historical records, same policy as session-21 leaderboard semantics. Cloud Run revision required for the API contract; see deploy below.
- Session 34 (2026-04-28): **Trip delete from History + Save-or-discard dialog on ride end.**
  - **Trip delete from History.** New `DELETE /v1/trips/:id` route in `services/mobile-api/src/routes/v1.ts` (`requireWriteUser` + write-bucket rate limit; returns 200 `{ deletedAt }` on success or 404 `NOT_FOUND` when the row isn't owned by the caller). Profile counters (`total_co2_saved_kg` etc.), `ride_impacts`, `ride_microlives`, badges, XP, and leaderboard snapshots are intentionally **not** unwound — past achievements and impact totals survive a delete (matches Strava behaviour, and the confirm copy says so).   - **Save-or-discard dialog on end-ride.** `apps/mobile/app/navigation.tsx` red Stop button now opens a 2-button `Alert.alert` ("Discard" destructive / "Save" default) instead of the previous Cancel+Confirm dialog. **Save** = current behaviour: queues `trip_end` + `trip_track` + optional `trip_share`, navigates to `/feedback` for XP / badges / microlives. **Discard** = `queueTripEnd('stopped', { discard: true })` queues **only** `trip_end` and early-returns — no `trip_track` (so nothing in History or stats), no `trip_share` (no community feed entry), no `/feedback` route (no `record_ride_impact`, no XP, no badges, no microlives, no community seconds). Discard navigates straight to `/route-planning`. Dialog dismissal (Android system back / tap outside): `onDismiss` callback fires the save handler — "save by default" per product spec; iOS forces a button choice. Removed the now-unused `useConfirmation` hook reference from this screen. Four new EN+RO i18n keys under `nav.*` (`endRideSaveTitle`, `endRideSaveMessage`, `endRideSave`, `endRideDiscard`); legacy `endRideConfirm*` keys retained for backward compat. No DB or Cloud Run change for this part — pure mobile. The orphaned `trips` row left server-side after a discard is harmless metadata (started_at, ended_at, end_reason='stopped') with zero downstream visibility.

- Session 33 (2026-04-27): **Pre-ride weather warning thresholds + cautionary wording.** Temperature warnings now skip entirely when the day stays in the 10–27°C comfort zone. Outside it, three independent rules can fire: cold (`remainingTempMin < 5°C`), heat (`remainingTempMax > 30°C` — new `'heat'` warning type), and big swing (`remainingTempMax − remainingTempMin > 13°C`, up from the previous 5°C). - Session 33 (2026-04-27): **Hide anonymous users from leaderboards.** Anonymous (pre-signup) sessions could appear in the City Heartbeat "Top Contributors" list and the Neighborhood Safety Leaderboard with empty `display_name` (handle_new_user trigger seeded `auto_share_rides = true` for everyone). - Session 33 (2026-04-27): **Trip-record idempotency.** Diagnosed why History showed the same trip multiple times: server had zero idempotency on `POST /trips/start` and `POST /trips/track`, so any client retry (10s `MUTATION_SYNC_TIMEOUT_MS` shorter than slow-uplink commit time, app-killed-mid-sync `recoverSyncingMutations`, dropped response packet, `useAppKilledRecovery` re-enqueue) would create a second `trip_tracks` row — and `getTripHistory` reads from `trip_tracks`. Fix is server-side because the network is unreliable. Migration `202604270002_trip_idempotency.sql` deduped existing `trip_tracks` (kept the row with the longest `gps_trail` per `trip_id`, tie-break `created_at` DESC), added `UNIQUE(trip_id)` on `trip_tracks`, added `trips.client_trip_id` + partial `UNIQUE(user_id, client_trip_id) WHERE client_trip_id IS NOT NULL` (legacy NULL rows allowed). `submissions.ts`: `startTripRecord` now upserts on `(user_id, client_trip_id)` so retries return the existing trip's id; `saveTripTrack` upserts on `trip_id` so retries overwrite the latest GPS trail rather than insert a duplicate. Migration applied via Supabase MCP (140 trip_tracks, 0 dupes remaining; 259 trips). Cloud Run revision `defpedal-api-00069-p7t` serving 100% traffic, `/health` 200. Mobile-side recovery paths (`useAppKilledRecovery`, stale-closure in `queueTripEnd`) are now safe by construction — no client changes needed.

(1) Upvote/downvote voting: `POST /v1/hazards/:id/vote` with `requireFullUser` auth (anonymous rejected 403), client speaks `up`/`down` and server maps to existing `confirm`/`deny` on `hazard_validations` (no schema collision).
